  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c35b6de8-5344-4147-8684-db7fd84ac271'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_1308831185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308831185" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1308831185?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=not-another-love-triangle">not-another-love-triangle</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308831185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9634440488383103287">Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/blood-bound/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>: <br/><br/>Owing a favor to a vampire is pretty much always going to be asking for trouble. Stefan, a vampire who’s been a help and even a friend to Mercy Thompson, calls her at three a.m. to go witness his confrontation with a new vampire in town. But Stefan gives Mercy his word of honor that she won’t be hurt, and asks her to shapeshift into her coyote form to accompany him. The new vampire, Cory Littleton, has a rather mundane name, but his nature is anything c</span>
  <span id="freeText9634440488383103287" style="display:none">Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/blood-bound/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>: <br /><br />Owing a favor to a vampire is pretty much always going to be asking for trouble. Stefan, a vampire who’s been a help and even a friend to Mercy Thompson, calls her at three a.m. to go witness his confrontation with a new vampire in town. But Stefan gives Mercy his word of honor that she won’t be hurt, and asks her to shapeshift into her coyote form to accompany him. The new vampire, Cory Littleton, has a rather mundane name, but his nature is anything commonplace: there is a demon inside of Littleton, and it’s not entirely clear whether the vampire is controlling the demon or is possessed by him. <br /><br />In any case, their meeting turns out to be fraught with danger and death, since Littleton possesses demonic-enhanced sorcerous powers that make him extremely dangerous to everyone in town, including vampires and werewolves as well as humans. As Mercy, Stefan and other vampires and werewolves combine to try to track down and kill or neutralize Littleton, it becomes apparent that there are some characters with a hidden agenda whose goals may not align with Mercy’s and humanity’s best interests. <br /><br /><i>Blood Bound</i>, the second book in the <i>Mercy Thompson</i> series, is a strong urban fantasy and mystery that builds on the world Patricia Briggs created in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71811.Moon_Called__Mercy_Thompson___1_" title="Moon Called (Mercy Thompson, #1) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Moon Called</a>. It’s bursting at the seams with vampires and werewolves, with a few fae characters for additional flavor, as well as Mercy herself, who is a “walker” and can turn into a coyote at will. Somehow Mercy, a hard-working, down-to-earth automobile mechanic, once again ends up in the middle of serious trouble, as the vampires and werewolves try to sort out the mystery involving Littleton, who’s leaving a trail of bodies behind him with a complete disregard for vampire rules.<br /><br />The one failure for me in <i>Blood Bound</i> is its subplot involving the overused love triangle trope, as Mercy continues to waffle between two werewolves who are each determined to make her their mate. Worse, there are hints that this might be turning into what might be best described as a three-pronged love trident, since now there are actually three different paranormal males interested in Mercy.<br /><br />Vampire society and culture take center stage in <i>Blood Bound</i>, as Mercy visits not only the main vampire compound but some of their personal dwellings, at great risk to herself. Briggs has created a detailed, layered world, with some intriguing twists on vampire characteristics and the standard mythology. The capabilities and shortcomings of Mercy and other supernatural beings, initially simply interesting facts, resurface later in the story and play a role in the development of the plot in a highly satisfying way. The plot and the underlying mystery in <i>Blood Bound</i> are a clear step above that in the first volume, <i>Moon Called</i>.<br /><br />Content notes: Lots of death and violence, but the gore factor isn't overwhelming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9634440488383103287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer927612565607613811">✘ <b>Now You See Me Now You Don't Express Buddy Read</b> (NYSMNYDEBR™) with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521360596' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nafeeza</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881262944' rel='nofollow noopener'>Layla</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871545761' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ange</a> ✘<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>☠ <b>DNF at 21%</b> <i>*pats her little self on the exoskeleton for making it that far*</i><br/><br/><b>Okay</b>, I was going to do the <b>Cut the Crap Thing</b> (CtCT™), but I just noticed the cover for this book and am consequently <b>slightly pissed off</b>, so this might take longer than originally planned. You're welcome.<br/><br/><b>That bloody shrimping cover</b>! What the bloody shrimping fish?! Why the holy barnacle does Mercy have to <b>display her boobs</b> li</span>
  <span id="freeText927612565607613811" style="display:none">✘ <b>Now You See Me Now You Don't Express Buddy Read</b> (NYSMNYDEBR™) with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521360596" rel="nofollow noopener">Nafeeza</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881262944" rel="nofollow noopener">Layla</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871545761" rel="nofollow noopener">Ange</a> ✘<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>☠ <b>DNF at 21%</b> <i>*pats her little self on the exoskeleton for making it that far*</i><br><br><b>Okay</b>, I was going to do the <b>Cut the Crap Thing</b> (CtCT™), but I just noticed the cover for this book and am consequently <b>slightly pissed off</b>, so this might take longer than originally planned. You're welcome.<br><br><b>That bloody shrimping cover</b>! What the bloody shrimping fish?! Why the holy barnacle does Mercy have to <b>display her boobs</b> like that?! Because her being a mechanic makes her less feminine, and she has to reassert her <b>womanly womanhood</b> by flaunting her freaking assets?! Just in case the readers <b>have a doubt</b> as to whether she is male of female? Or is it just that is it <b>super HAWT</b> (both literally and figuratively) in Washington State and our dear girl just NEEDS to keep her work coveralls open at all times? You know, <b>for the sake of ventilation and stuff</b>? Right. I'm sure that's what this is about. Damn I hate that kind of crap. The cover would have been <s>just as hot</s> way hotter, had Mercy shown <b>just a little cleavage</b>. Because, YES, a chick can look hot in coveralls even when she is NOT <b>showing off her boobs</b>! This probably comes as a shock, I know. I'm sorry I had to break it to you <b>so brutally</b>, my Little Barnacles, but you couldn't be left in the dark any longer. Your <b>mental sanity</b> was at stake here, whether you realize it or not. Someone had to do something about it!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450598464ra/17447744.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Why you're very welcome, my dears. I absolutely lurve that cute kitty, by the way. You know my tastes so well, it's touching, really <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[*summons Fleet Admiral DaShrimp* "DaShrimp, nuke those Silly Barnacles NOW! No one throws cute kitties at me and gets away with it unscathed!" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i> <br><br><b>Anyway</b>, I know exactly what happened here. This was yet an <b>evilly cunning plan</b> to demolish a book by its cover, courtesy of the lovely people at Ace. They've been doing <b>such a wonderful job of it</b> with Ilona Andrews' books, they just couldn't resist the temptation here! They just had to <b>try and ruin</b> yet another series via (choose all <s>that apply</s>) pathetic/ridiculous/eyeroll-worthy/worthless book cover! The problem is, Ms Briggs <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[bless her little heart for being such a devoted Kate Daniels fan <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is no Ilona Andrews, which means <b>Immutable Law of the Universe</b> #1 (ILotU1™) doesn't apply to her. Yeah, <b>life sucks</b>, I know. Sorry? What? "What is ILotU1™," you ask? Simply this: the crappier the cover, the gloriouser the book. The Andrews recently passed the <b>Blue Abs From Hell Cover Test</b> (BAFHCT™) with flying colors, by the way. And if that isn't the proof that ILotU1™ was created just for them, I don't know what is. <b>Okayyyyy</b>, I seem to vaguely recall that there was originally a point to this paragraph. There must have been something, right? Because everything I say <b>always has a point</b>, right? Right. So glad we blissfully agree, my Little Barnacles. Oh yes, I remember now! The point to this paragraph, I mean! Here it is: <b>Patricia Briggs is no Ilona Andrews and this book sucks just as much as its cover</b>! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484868493i/21762533.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>As you Lovely Decapods</b> very well know, I am quite the <s>special snowflake</s> dedicated <b>masochist</b>. Yes, it is true, I love to read <s>crap</s> stuff I know I will <s>want to kill dead</s> not necessarily enjoy. But what happened here is <b>not my fault</b>. Oh no, absolutely not. Because you see, I <b>loved</b> book 1 in this series SO much, I decided to do the <b>Pre Emptive DNFing Thing</b> (PEDT™) on this one. Which loosely translates to: "I'd rather die at the hands of a thousand <b>lethally ferocious dinoflagellates</b> than continue with this series." More or less. But then <b>Deviously Cunning Angela</b> (DCA™) happened. She put a gun to my lovely little head and made me read this <s>thing</s> book, or else... Horrific thing to do, is it not? Such <b>lowly, disrespectful behavior</b> coming from someone with such despicable book taste wouldn't have been tolerated back in the <b>good old days</b> of my lovely dictatorship. This is pretty disgraceful, if you ask me. I'm telling you, my Tiny Athropods, it is no wonder that this world is <b>going to hell</b>, and that some of you chose to vote for Trumpy instead of electing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8180684.Craig_Schaefer" rel="nofollow noopener">Craig Schaefer is Slightly Awesome</a> as POTUS #45 *shakes head in desperation* But I ever so slightly digress. So I found myself in the <b>despicable position</b> of having to <s>DNF</s> read this <s>thing</s> book against my better judgement. And here we are.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487880435i/22060717.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[This is were the supposedly crap-cutting review supposedly begins]<br><br><b>Sooooooo</b>, I only read three chapters of this <b>fascinatingly delightful</b> little book because:<br><br>① <b>It's boring to death</b>. And it's boring to death. Yeah, that too. 3 chapters = 21% of this book = 61 pages in Briggs world = 1,225,586 pages in the real world. Give or take a few hundred thousand pages. <br><br>② <b>The blah blah blah crap is strong in that one</b>. Most of the above mentioned <s>three chapters</s> 1,225,586 pages are filled to the brim with 1/useless dialogues, 2/pointless ramblings and 3/meaningless descriptions of meaningless things. Such a treat.<br><br>③ The <b>Gloriously Captivating Relationship Crap Extravaganza</b> (GCRCE™), aka the stuff I liked best:<br><br>➽ There are no <b>Love Triangles of Doom and Destruction</b> (LToDaD™) in this world, oh no, that would be way too lame. Ms Briggs has <b>Love Quadrangles of Annihilation and Obliteration</b> (LQoAaO™) instead. It is much, MUCH cooler.<br>➽ <b>Mercy Thompson</b> is such a cool, independent young woman that she is very logically defined by her <b>exponentially multiplying suitors</b>. All she does, all she is, seems to be dictated by the <s>dull, boring, flat douchebags</s> delicious males in her life. And that is just SO cool. <b>Go feminism! Go</b>!<br>➽ The LQoAaO™ thing is <b>super exciting</b>. Which is logical. There are, after all, three <s>lacklustre losers</s> hot dudes lusting after Mercy Dear here: <b>one</b> is a doctor (wow) who wants Mercy Dear for her <b>reproductive organs</b> (how positively charming), <b>another</b> is her neighbour who takes her on hot dates with his <b>teenage daughter</b> tagging along (thrilling) and the <b>last one</b> is a vamp with a Mystery Machine à la <b>Scooby Doo</b> (how exquisitely modern of him), who likes to <s>play dead</s> sleep in Mercy Dear's bedroom closet once in a while (riveting). What can I say? <b>I'm jealous</b>. I'd gladly give up all the <s>sex slaves</s> cultural attachés in my harem if it meant having <b>just one go</b> at one of these <s>cardboard-like idiots</s> luscious babes. Yes, absolutely, this is the <b>truthful truth</b>. These <s>uninteresting fools</s> most edible guys here are <u>that</u> <b>irresistibly irresistible</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487884768i/22061252._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Is it really? Strange. Have you had your bullshit-o-meter checked like I told you the other day, Spidey dear? I personally smell no BS in a 12,000 mile radius from this review.</i> <br><br><b>The End</b>.<br><br>» And the moral of this <b>I Have Done the Patricia Briggs Thing FOUR FREAKING TIMES Now even Subaquatic Masochists Have their Limits I am Done Done Done Crappy Non Review</b> (IHDtPBTFFTNeSMHtLIaDDDCNR™) is: Ange is getting a <b>penance read</b> for putting me through two successive <s>pieces of crap</s> slightly unenjoyable books. She will therefore be held at <s>gunpoint</s> <b>shrimp pincers</b> until she turns the last page of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22743827.The_Long_Way_Down__Daniel_Faust___1_" title="The Long Way Down (Daniel Faust, #1) by Craig Schaefer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Long Way Down</a>. I have the weird feeling I got <b>somewhat ripped off</b> here, and that she got the better part of the deal. <b>Don't know why</b>.<br><br>✎ <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074849414" rel="nofollow noopener">Moon Called</a> ★★<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>You Silly Barnacles</b> pretty much all love this series, don't you? Right. That's what I thought.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487862533ra/22058715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wait. No</b>. Why the shrimping fish would I deprive the world of my <b>most glorious persona</b> when YOU are the ones who keep reading books wrong?! I shall therefore stay right here and continue to graciously enlighten you <b>Tiny Arthropods of the Despicable Book Taste</b> (TAotDBT™) one crappy read at a time. You are very much welcome.<br><br>►► Not so full <b>My Dear Ms Briggs I Am Sure You Are a Wonderful Person But I am Officially Done Done Done with your Books Yay Go Me Crappy Mini Non Review</b> (MDMBIASYAaWPBIaODDDwyBYGMCMNR™) to come.<br><br>✉ <i>A very private message to my friendly neighbourhood trolls: don't even think about it. Unless you want to die a slow, horrible, painful death, that is.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_689121650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689121650" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689121650?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/6975982-blood-bound">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=2020-audio-book-challenge">2020-audio-book-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689121650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16642039835106688683"><b><br/>Re-read for the 3rd time April 2nd, 2020. I notice more to love with every re-read! <br/><br/>Re-read March 21st 2017. Even better the 2nd time around!<br/><br/>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Blood Bound, the second installment in the Mercy Thompson series has me officially addicted! <br/><br/>This begins as Mercy’s friend, Stephan the vampire, calls in a favor owed. Little does she know that repayment puts her and the pack in grave danger, not something Stephan intended, either. What they stumble upon is a powerful threat that Mercy can’t let st</span>
  <span id="freeText16642039835106688683" style="display:none"><b><br />Re-read for the 3rd time April 2nd, 2020. I notice more to love with every re-read! <br /><br />Re-read March 21st 2017. Even better the 2nd time around!<br /><br />4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Blood Bound, the second installment in the Mercy Thompson series has me officially addicted! <br /><br />This begins as Mercy’s friend, Stephan the vampire, calls in a favor owed. Little does she know that repayment puts her and the pack in grave danger, not something Stephan intended, either. What they stumble upon is a powerful threat that Mercy can’t let stand and before you know it, she’s waist high in dangerous vampire politics. Trying to distinguish the truth from subterfuge is difficult and vital if Mercy plans on staying alive. <br /><br />Like most UF’s I’ve picked up, Mercy Thompson has a new mystery/problem to overcome with each book and also a continuing story arc that progresses, bit by bit in each installment. The new mystery is the vampire/sorcerer-crazy with massive amounts of power and wicked intent. There were parts of this story that genuinely made heart race from fear! Vampires are scary (and not sparkly), especially in the end! <br /><br />I love Mercedes Thompson! She’s intelligent, a master of reading complicated situations and handling them with care. She reads between the lines and looks beyond the obvious, making her a force to be reckoned with. <br /><br />The continuing arc is the romance, and it’s the part I love best! There is sort of a love triangle with Adam and Samuel in the mix, but not in an irritating way. Samuel has decided to stay in Washington, more specifically, with Mercy, when she’s made it clear she’s not interested. Samuel makes it clear he is. He was her first love but finding out exactly why he was interested her sent her running years ago. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mercy could bear his children, ones that would have the potential to be born werewolves, and therefore Samuel would have children he wouldn’t outlive. Finding out this was more a motivator than love broke Mercy’s heart at sixteen.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Now that Mercy looks back, though, she doesn’t regret the situation, because she realizes now that Samuel, as dominant as he is, would’ve wrapped her up in a protective cocoon and stifled her independent spirit. <br /><br />Adam, the Alpha of the pack is domineering but still respects and appreciates Mercy for who she is rather than what she can do. He’s attracted to Mercy the woman, and isn’t looking for a pack brood mare. Mercy knew that Adam claimed her as his mate but thinks this was in name only, just for protection. A lone “walker” coyote like Mercy without protection would be a target for the wolves and probably wouldn’t last long. A few things happen that make it apparent that Adam’s “claim” has more power and sincerity behind it. This puts Mercy in a bind with Samuel back. Poor Mercy, *not* with two handsome, possessive, alpha males after her! <br /><br />This was an exciting, and sometimes frightening read. Parts at the end gave me chills and goose bumps! I tried to force myself to put it aside just for my commutes. Something I wasn’t at all successful at! I’ve just finished book three: Iron Kissed, and I have to say the series just gets better! <br /> <br />I loved Lorelei King as the narrator. She has a warm, rich voice with a slightly sarcastic and humorous tone that I find perfect for Mercy. Her male voices are also quite good, as well, and the story flowed seamlessly because of it. I highly recommend the audio version! <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/08/review-blood-bound-mercy-thompson-2-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16642039835106688683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_38217416" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38217416" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38217416?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of urban fantasy, werewolf fiction, great heroines</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=werewolf">werewolf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=shapeshifter">shapeshifter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=demon">demon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38217416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14707683560014276708">There is something so wonderful about Patricia Briggs's writing for this reader. She is able to create a world in which I am completely drawn in, but she writes with such simple elegance. Without a doubt, this is my favorite urban fantasy series so far.<br/><br/>Mercy Thompson is the kind of heroine that earns my devotion. She is so brave, but has the same fears and uncertainties that us readers have. She wants a simple life, even though she's a walker, a coyote shapeshifter, who is up to her neck in were</span>
  <span id="freeText14707683560014276708" style="display:none">There is something so wonderful about Patricia Briggs's writing for this reader. She is able to create a world in which I am completely drawn in, but she writes with such simple elegance. Without a doubt, this is my favorite urban fantasy series so far.<br /><br />Mercy Thompson is the kind of heroine that earns my devotion. She is so brave, but has the same fears and uncertainties that us readers have. She wants a simple life, even though she's a walker, a coyote shapeshifter, who is up to her neck in werewolf politics, not to mention vampire and fae issues. She has to go to work the next day even after staying up all night, dealing with demon-possessed vampires and the like, knowing that some of her close friends might be dead. I think Ms. Briggs has really tapped into the wellspring of what pulls me in as a reader in this genre. She is able to give me a fantastic world that is imbued with the real life things, and the combination is very satisfying.<br /><br />Mercy could not be more admirable. Not a perfect person, but who is? Nevertheless, she has qualities that earn my respect. She is strong, and loving, empathetic, and willing to do the dirty jobs. Her courage in a truly harrowing situation spoke to me. She could have just moved on, and took things as they ended, but her conscience told her she had to finish things. Which she did, despite her fear, her guilt about doing something that went against her code, and her disgust at what she had to to. And Mercy is surrounded by men (wolves/vamps) who are used to exerting their dominance, but she navigates her way through this testosterone-laden world without losing her sense of self, or control over her own life.<br /><br />The men in this series. Oh, the men. Adam is the keeper of my heart. I just love that man. I believe he is the right man for Mercy, hands down. The chemistry between Mercy and Adam is divine. There is a naturalness to their relationship, full of tension, but so organic. I loved all their scenes together, reading the subtext of their complex relationship. How Adam has to suppress his compelling power as the alpha, but his feelings for Mercy make it difficult. How Mercy wants to submit, but doesn't want to, at the same time, out of fear of losing herself and disappearing into the pack hierarchy. So intense! And then there's Samuel. He was Mercy's first boyfriend, the man she almost mated to. He still wants her, even more than ever. But he knows he messed up the first time, and his fight to give Mercy the choice of who she wants, takes its toll on him. And then there's his pain at what he has lost, and fears he will never have again.<br /><br />The vampires in this series are scary! They are predators, pure and simple. They have powers that make them formidable enemies and uneasy allies. Mercy's 'so-called' friend Stefan has an ambiguosity to him that is inherent because of his being a powerful vampire, but at the same time, having a humaneness that the other vampires lack. He's one of the good ones, but he's still a predator at the end of the day. Mercy knows she's in over her head when she has to deal with the vampires, and particularly a demon-possessed sorcerer vampire. But Mercy has the power to resist the vampires to a degree that the other preternaturals lack, even though her small size and lack of strength as a coyote shifter leaves her at a disadvantage. There are parts in this book where I felt the tension like a knife edge. The evil that these creatures were capable of was always clear. Yet some hid it behind an urbane facade. <br /><br />But more than anything, I love the wolves. The pack dynamics are utterly fascinating. The basic and primal nature of the wolves always played a factor in how Mercy dealt with Samuel, Adam, Bran (the leader of all the werewolves in North America), Warren (Adam's third, a good friend of Mercy), and some of the other wolves in this book. I felt envy that this was not real. But at the same time, I'm not sure I could handle being in love with a werewolf, and knowing that his control is what keeps him from eating or killing you, if that inner wolf nature takes full control. Not to mention dealing with the dicey pack politics that Mercy gets sucked into, despite her desire to do her own thing.<br /><br />I'm gushing. I know I am. I can't help it. I love this book, and this series. I think I will have restrain myself from speeding my way through it too fast. I don't think I could handle having to wait a long time for the next books in the series, then!<br /><br />If you're looking for a really good urban fantasy series with a heroine that you will fall in love with, I recommend this series. If you are into werewolf fiction, you are really missing out if you don't read this one. These werewolves are the best in fiction (in my opinion). Thumbs way up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14707683560014276708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115087027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115087027" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115087027?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=shifter">shifter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115087027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18321932498177466991"><br/>The second book in the Mercy installment centers upon the vampires. Stefen, good friend and Scooby-lovin, t-shirt wearing vamp, calls in a favor. Favors among the supernatural are always tricky. When Mercy goes with him to a hotel to meet a suspicious new vampire, they both get more than they bargained for. Yucky stuff follows, but Stefen has a different memory of the horror in the hotel. Mercy must share her memory with the vampire seethe in a bloody and creepy way so that the queen Marsilia do</span>
  <span id="freeText18321932498177466991" style="display:none"><br />The second book in the Mercy installment centers upon the vampires. Stefen, good friend and Scooby-lovin, t-shirt wearing vamp, calls in a favor. Favors among the supernatural are always tricky. When Mercy goes with him to a hotel to meet a suspicious new vampire, they both get more than they bargained for. Yucky stuff follows, but Stefen has a different memory of the horror in the hotel. Mercy must share her memory with the vampire seethe in a bloody and creepy way so that the queen Marsilia does not kill Stefen for bringing unwelcome attention to the vampires. From there, Mercy is kicked out of the action while the menfolk look for the crazy vampire, until the queen vampire contacts Mercy and lends her Andre after the men go missing.<br /><br />I'm really not a horror reader. Ever since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10583.Pet_Sematary" title="Pet Sematary by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Pet Sematary</a> when I was thirteen, I've stayed far away from the genre, only coming close when urban fantasy flirted with things that go bump in the night. Oh, and Sherri Tepper, who does the science fiction version of the creepy dark side of humanity. At any rate, this opens with Mercy trapped as a psychotic vampire kills someone in front of her and hardly lets up. Well, I say 'hardly lets up' because I felt like there was a lot of description about eating bloody people as well as general descriptions of blood, torture and killing. But perhaps Briggs needed the horror to keep readers awake, because in between events there is an unbelievable amount of info-dumping. In a side plot, a reporter hounds Mercy, and she ends up giving him a lecture and a half about werewolves, while in the main storyline, Mercy and the reader learn almost everything there is to know about vampire politics, vampire skills, sorcerers and demons. <br /><br />Characterization continues to be one of Briggs' stronger skills with Mercy being the most interesting voice. Plotting has interesting stops along the way, although the overall arc is almost identical to the first book. The editors must not have expected readers to have read book one, as much of chapters one through three review Mercy's identity, her history with Samuel and her recent history with Adam. The crazy vampire bites Mercy, which is an unpleasant bit of rape-foreshadowing. Once again, the book virtually fails the Bechdel test, with the exception of a brief conversation with Honey the werewolf and a grade-school girl who gives her a clue. Even Mercy's talks with an elderly female ghost is about men. It also introduces the idea that Stefen might also have an unusual affection for Mercy, competing with both Adam and Samuel for her attention. Apparently, I was wrong--to know Mercy <i>is</i> to love her. It is also becoming clear that while Mercy may be shuffled to the side by the wolves, she will usually be put into a position where she is 'forced' to circumvent them or to go off on her own. In this case, the crazy vampire was so strong, he "brought out the wolf" in everyone. This will become a theme through the series.<br /><br />This one does not hold up as well on re-read, for both personal and critical reasons. It was the book that had me considering giving up on the series, and if I wasn't such a completist, I probably wouldn't even have it on my shelves. Two stars and a half stars, rounding down for both the info-dumping and lukewarm gurrl-power message.<br /><br /><br />Re-read May 2016</span>
  <a data-text-id="18321932498177466991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_743755693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743755693" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743755693?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=adorable-alphas">adorable-alphas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=audio-challenge-2020">audio-challenge-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743755693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16058519861001425388">Re-read: Still 3.5 Stars <br/><br/>I'm still a little behind on the <a href='https://booksofmyheart.net/category/read-along/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Books of my Heart Read Along</a><a></a> but catching up fast. <br/><br/>I had forgotten everything from this book, literally everything. Vampire in league with a Demon you think I would have remembered something. Oh well. This was a solid read and I noticed a lot of repetition this time just in case you didn't remember stuff from the first book but other than that very nice read.<br/><br/>I forgot that all the guys love Mercy. Adam, Sam and Stephan she is pretty cool b</span>
  <span id="freeText16058519861001425388" style="display:none">Re-read: Still 3.5 Stars <br /><br />I'm still a little behind on the <a href="https://booksofmyheart.net/category/read-along/" rel="nofollow noopener">Books of my Heart Read Along</a><a></a> but catching up fast. <br /><br />I had forgotten everything from this book, literally everything. Vampire in league with a Demon you think I would have remembered something. Oh well. This was a solid read and I noticed a lot of repetition this time just in case you didn't remember stuff from the first book but other than that very nice read.<br /><br />I forgot that all the guys love Mercy. Adam, Sam and Stephan she is pretty cool but that is a lot of dudes longing for her. Wolfe again was a cool character and while I don't remember a lot about him I liked how he helped Mercy in the end. <br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“We'd spent years as adversaries, two predators sharing territory and a certain, unwelcome attraction. Somehow, during all those years I spent outwardly acquiescing to his demands while making sure I held my own, I'd won his respect. I'd had werewolves love me and hate me, but I'd never had one respect me before. Not even Samuel. Adam respected me enough to act on my suspicions. It meant a lot.”</i>
</b><br /><br />There is something about this series that I really like. I can’t seem to put my finger exactly on it whether it is the plethora of alpha males, the different supernatural creatures that are a little different than other series, the plot of the story or just Mercy herself. There is <i>something</i> that makes this fun and better than some of the other UF out there.<br /><br />I enjoyed Blood Born just as much as Moon Called. The world around Mercy is opening up and letting us in a little at a time. In this book, we get a better look into the life of Vampires and all the politics that go along with it. Stefan helped Mercy in moon called and now she wants to return the favor. But Stefan’s problem turns out being bigger than he first thought it might be. What’s worse than a vampire or a demon? How about a vampire possessed by a Demon. Yep, that is worse.<br /><br />The things I like about Mercy: She is strong willed and quick to react. She doesn’t sit and ho hum like some of the other characters in novels. She doesn’t have super strength or Buffy moves. She takes martial arts and can hold her own in a fight but isn’t a high flying kick ass superhero or anything. She is smart and uses her instincts to solve problems. Sure there is something a little magical about her but even she isn’t sure what that is. She is not perfect, she has so many trust issues and is afraid that giving into Adam or Samuel will mean that she will lose her in independent self. Mercy is self-aware, kind and doesn’t take herself too seriously. When push comes to shove Mercy pushes right back.<br /><br />Again the side characters are great. I really love Stefan, the vampire who is kinder than most but still a vampire. Getting a look into Samuel‘s character I started to like him more, don’t get me wrong I’m still team Adam all the way, but I get where Sam’s character is coming from and see that he truly cares for Mercy still. Adam, well *sigh* I love Adam. He is strong and protective, however he tries not to stand in Mercy’s way and let her be her own woman and help her friends. He trusts and respects her, he seems to know who she is and doesn’t try to change that. <br /><br />The Fae are definitely interesting, they are not the fairies of other books. They are dark, mysterious and seem to have a lot of power. Zee is my favorite, he is like a father to Mercy and I have to love that. Grumpy and cantankerous are just a bonus.<br /><br />The Demon possessed vampire story line was well thought out and scary enough. Mercy will go a long way for her friends. It was horrifying the depths of evil that seemed to be incorporated into the demon aspect and I was really scared for the characters in the story.<br /><br />All and all enjoyable and another nice addition to the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16058519861001425388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2295424-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305638929p2/2295424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70756616?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/2295424-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70756616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10985711241814788427">I’m beginning to understand why this series has such a large fan base!<br/><br/>The first book in this series certainly was promising but I found that a combination of Mercy’s dry tone narrative and a lack of action made it hard for me to get into the story. <br/>This time around I had a little trouble in the beginning, but soon after I got drawn into an engaging and exciting story in where the ever helpful Mercy gets sucked into vampire business (no pun intended). In the mean while, we learn more about Briggs</span>
  <span id="freeText10985711241814788427" style="display:none">I’m beginning to understand why this series has such a large fan base!<br /><br />The first book in this series certainly was promising but I found that a combination of Mercy’s dry tone narrative and a lack of action made it hard for me to get into the story. <br />This time around I had a little trouble in the beginning, but soon after I got drawn into an engaging and exciting story in where the ever helpful Mercy gets sucked into vampire business (no pun intended). In the mean while, we learn more about Briggs' world of vampires, Fae and werewolves. <br /><br />The world Briggs has built is absolutely fantastic and so real! And she does not glorify her supernatural characters. Her vampires are scary and unpredictable, the werewolves are bound by their hierarchic rules and old-fashioned prejudices and the Fae are not to be trusted. And still we feel for them, fear for them en get to love them.<br /><br />I’m really starting to love Mercy. I'm beginning to get the Mercy-Adam-Samuel triangle. But I must say: my favorite by far was Stefan! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10985711241814788427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_309769138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309769138" />
    <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog"><img alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309769138?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-not-mm">what-not-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-modern-fantasy">what-modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-vampires">what-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-danger-danger-wilma-robinson">what-danger-danger-wilma-robinson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-shifters">what-shifters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309769138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16719957158082509969">Ugh. I am so unhappy with Ms. Briggs. She created an intelligent, strong, interesting protagonist; a mostly believable world; and engaging supporting characters. Her writing is smooth and keeps you turning the page, wanting to see where the plot is headed. But the sexist drivel just makes me want to puke. On the surface it doesn't seem to be sexist: Mercy abhors the way women are treated in the werewolf pack; she is strong and resourceful and of course has to save the day. But when I delved deep</span>
  <span id="freeText16719957158082509969" style="display:none">Ugh. I am so unhappy with Ms. Briggs. She created an intelligent, strong, interesting protagonist; a mostly believable world; and engaging supporting characters. Her writing is smooth and keeps you turning the page, wanting to see where the plot is headed. But the sexist drivel just makes me want to puke. On the surface it doesn't seem to be sexist: Mercy abhors the way women are treated in the werewolf pack; she is strong and resourceful and of course has to save the day. But when I delved deeper, I realized that this is the annoying Heinlein-esque sexism: you know the guy is a jerk and you know better but let's just humor him. The reality is that in humoring, he gets all the power and control. Just because you're going along voluntarily doesn't make it okay. <br /><br />The women in this society are virtually slaves, she freely admits it. The men have magic that can control women and force them to submit, particularly sexually. Mercy knows this and tries to distance herself somewhat but she keeps getting sucked in. She even lives with one of them who wants her. She is constantly in the middle of a tug-of-war with several studs wanting her at once and she doesn't do anything about it. Instead, she continually ends up trying to calm them down by being meek and submissive around them. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong: I believe the society she's created is realistic. It makes perfect sense that people who struggle with a primal beast would succumb to the feral hierarchy directed by testosterone. What I have a problem with is that the character not only tolerates it, she keeps getting herself sucked in. It's the stereotypical bodice-busting romance story of a woman who wants a dangerous man who doesn't treat her well but she knows she can save him. It's disgusting. Why can't these strong women like strong guys who are comfortable in their masculinity and their status in society who treat them well and who respect the woman's own strength and power?<br /><br />I almost stopped reading when I got to a line that went something like, "You know you submitted because you wanted to." The line was referring to a situation where this strong woman was mentally and emotionally controlled through magic and almost forced to have sex against her will (they were interupted which broke the spell) but it was okay because he didn't really have control of his magic because he wanted her so much and secretly she really wanted it? Are you kidding me?!<br /><br />The worst part is this: (This spoiler is about character relationships and not about plot or conflict resolution.)<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />At one point Mercy decides she has to decide between one of these two uncontrolled werewolves that want her: the one that almost raped her and the one that hurt her horribly in the past. She is completely horrified, though, by the vampire who is always gentle and kind to her, never takes her for granted, protects her when necessary but allows her to be strong and powerful, and in general is a perfect gentleman. The reason is that in a crisis he had another vampire kill two half-crazed, near-death minions of a third vampire, minions who would undoubtedly have been killed anyway. It really was a mercy killing, which he did so that Mercy wouldn't be hunted down and slaughtered by the rest of the vampires. <br /><br />She tolerates horrific violence and human rights violations by the werewolves because it's the way they are but she is completely repulsed and terrified of a vampire who will not kill because he knows Mercy doesn't want him to but ends up having to off to near-dead half-vampire/half-humans to save her life? This makes NO sense to me and is a very disturbing set of ethics. I'm not saying she should necessarily be okay with the vampire but her reaction to his wrongs are seriously wonky in relation to her tolerance of the wolves' actions.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'd give it a one for this sexism alone but I did finish it because it was compelling. And I love that vampire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16719957158082509969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/573682353" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101057810" href="/book/show/9890766-blood-bound">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=skimmed">skimmed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573682353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17991485449395736688">Okay friends...I'm sorry, but this is it. I don't plan to follow this series any farther. This is not because Patricia Briggs is a bad writer. It's not because the idea behind the book is bad or the plot is bad.<br/><br/>Then why? Many of you probably already know if you've read any of my reviews. The plot, the story idea, the characters are there, but they are constantly smothered by Mercy going on and on about her hormones when she's around either of 2 alpha werewolves. It's about this continually overw</span>
  <span id="freeText17991485449395736688" style="display:none">Okay friends...I'm sorry, but this is it. I don't plan to follow this series any farther. This is not because Patricia Briggs is a bad writer. It's not because the idea behind the book is bad or the plot is bad.<br /><br />Then why? Many of you probably already know if you've read any of my reviews. The plot, the story idea, the characters are there, but they are constantly smothered by Mercy going on and on about her hormones when she's around either of 2 alpha werewolves. It's about this continually overwhelming the said story and dominating the book.<br /><br />I wanted to like this book as I'm always looking for a good UF but FOR ME..I repeat FOR ME this is just more a PNR (paranormal romance) than it is UF. Mercy comments on how "hot" here vampire "friend" is even though she's up front about how deadly that can be. Like SO MANY OTHER female protagonists from Stephanie Plum to Dagny Taggart she can't seem to decide on one man. This can be a fatal flaw for a book if you (the reader) detest long constant dialogues, monologues and any other kind of "logues" taking up 50%+ of the book.<br /><br />I'm sure the parts of this book that have brought about my dropping the series are the very parts that will keep some reading (I almost named a friend here who I know loves romances paranormal and otherwise...but I don't want to get into trouble).<br /><br />If you like this and it's your cup of tea, enjoy. I'm through, gone, don't plan to follow the series any farther.<br /><br />At least I didn't buy this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17991485449395736688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1361875058" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15687054250581931707"><b>2018 Review</b>:<br/>As I continue my reading journey down memory lane, I realize that right here in book two is where Patricia Briggs and I go separate ways regarding who we want to see Mercy shacked up with. This was the book that to me said, “Go vampires! Stefan all the way!”<br/><br/>You see, I’m just not into being bossed around. Eldest child, bossy in my own right, don’t need to butt heads with some stubborn werewolf every damn day. In fact, every now and then, my gentleman friend will ask me, “Not a vampire</span>
  <span id="freeText15687054250581931707" style="display:none"><b>2018 Review</b>:<br />As I continue my reading journey down memory lane, I realize that right here in book two is where Patricia Briggs and I go separate ways regarding who we want to see Mercy shacked up with. This was the book that to me said, “Go vampires! Stefan all the way!”<br /><br />You see, I’m just not into being bossed around. Eldest child, bossy in my own right, don’t need to butt heads with some stubborn werewolf every damn day. In fact, every now and then, my gentleman friend will ask me, “Not a vampire yet?” Now I think he mostly asks just to get me to nibble his neck, but he has obviously been studying my bookshelves and has recognized a significant theme.<br /><br />I’m not sure what the lure of the vampire dark side is for me. But it’s there and I plan to indulge it again in 2019.<br /><br /><b>Original review</b>:<br /><br />More Stefan and more vampires. Yay! And these are dangerous vampires, not cutesy ones. Mercy faces them all bravely and it turns out that her feminine ways of doing things are more effective than all the macho werewolf snarling in the world. My impressions of Stefan (a character I like very much) are morphing—he is changing from a supernatural buddy into someone tall, dark, and dangerous!<br /><br />The more I learn about Briggs’ paranormal world, the more I like it. She takes the stereotypical vampires, werewolves and fae and does interesting things with them. Despite the changes, it is fairly easy to keep up with who can do what and why—but the explanations are worked into the book well, not as annoying info dumps.<br /><br />I guess I’m older than the usual target audience for urban fantasy—I’m well beyond the stage of thinking that competing men, vying for my attention, is a wonderful romantic thing. So I’ll be very glad if Mercy chooses one of them in the next book or two and we can get on with sub-plots that are of more interest to me. Fingers crossed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15687054250581931707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3148740001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3148740001" />
    <a title="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures"><img alt="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463631966p2/7742509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3148740001?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" href="/user/show/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures">Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/6975982-blood-bound">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=2020-audiobook-challenge">2020-audiobook-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=fav-vampire-books">fav-vampire-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=paperbacks-i-own">paperbacks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=nook-own-library">nook-own-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=audiobooks-i-own">audiobooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=fav-shifter-books">fav-shifter-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=fav-magic-books">fav-magic-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3148740001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3472009717161778277"><b>Blood Bound</b> is book two in the <i>Mercy Thompson</i> series by Patricia Briggs. Each book continues the ongoing adventure with our coyote shifter, Mercy. It continues to develop the characters, relationships, and world. <br/><br/>I LOVE this series. I LOVE Mercy! She’s a kick-ass heroine. She knows she shouldn’t play with the big boys, but she can’t help wanting to help those she cares about. <br/><br/>In <b>
  <i>Blood Bound</i>
</b> we dive into the dean of the Vampires and learn about their structure. Mercy gets involved with the se</span>
  <span id="freeText3472009717161778277" style="display:none"><b>Blood Bound</b> is book two in the <i>Mercy Thompson</i> series by Patricia Briggs. Each book continues the ongoing adventure with our coyote shifter, Mercy. It continues to develop the characters, relationships, and world. <br><br>I LOVE this series. I LOVE Mercy! She’s a kick-ass heroine. She knows she shouldn’t play with the big boys, but she can’t help wanting to help those she cares about. <br><br>In <b>
  <i>Blood Bound</i>
</b> we dive into the dean of the Vampires and learn about their structure. Mercy gets involved with the seethe and a demon-riding vampire. She handles herself well in that she uses her connections and knowledge to locate the threat and save her friends. She’s capable and smart. <br><br>The relationships between the characters are intense. We dig deeper into exploring the Vampire world and her friendship with Stefan which is a forbidden relationship for both of them. Biggs isn’t afraid to show the amazing side of the vampires, but also the darker and edgier side. We also dig into Adams pack. I love the friendship Mercy has with Warren. I like that we learn how Adam and Warren became friends and how Warren joined the pack. We see that many don’t like Warren’s sexual preference and treat him as less or they want him out. We also see that most in the pack only tolerate Mercy, but when things get dicy she can dominate them, even Adams’ second. Mercy feels that she is despised and that a coyote has no place in a pack, but as the reader we see that she does have a place, but that she just hasn’t seen it yet. <br><br>The developing romance or romances. I am not one for love triangles and since I've read this series many times I know which direction Mercy goes, but here at the beginning we see that Mercy is not one to lead anyone on, so what will she do when her X, Samuel, comes back into her life. He’s the man she was going to be with until she found out the real reason he wanted her now she’s not sure what she feels for him. Then theirs Adam the packs Alpha and his claim that she is his mate. My heart broke for Samuel when he reveals the truth about what happened in Texas. Then theirs Adam and the developing feelings Mercy has for him. Oh my that work-out scene with Adam. Swooning! We see how she feels about Adam, but also her struggle with being controlled or losing her free will. She grew up around the wolves. She knows their structure, how the Alphas are and she’s scared. Briggs isn’t afraid to leave us in a love triangle with Adam and Samuel at the end. What will Mercy do?<br><br>We also get to learn more about what Mercy can do and why Vampires don’t like her kind. I enjoyed learning more about the coyote shifter and what her abilities are. No one really knows what she can do or they know, but don’t tell it all and just give us and Mercy bites of information. It’s these kind of tidbits of knowledge that I love and enjoy how the author weaves them in. <br><br><b>Narration:</b> Lorelei King is a spectacular narrater. She does a wonderful job with the storyline and characters. I love her voices for everyone.<br><br>This is one of my favorite series and I’ve re-read and listened to it multiple times. It’s a delight and each time is always like the first. I highly recommend this Urban Fantasy series. Don’t hesitate to pick it up.<br><br><b>Rate: 4.5 Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://angelsguiltypleasures.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466193893i/19451911.jpg" width="400" height="100" alt="angelsgp-seethisreview-blure" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3472009717161778277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1636817949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636817949" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1636817949?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22908716-blood-bound">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636817949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15328917638979868715">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a><br/><br/>I have so much love for this series! This was my second time reading this book and I can honestly say that I liked it just as much as I did the first and maybe even a bit more. One thing that I enjoy about re-reading books in series that I love is seeing how many things have changed for the characters. I love how some of the groundwork for future events takes root in earlier books.<br/><br/>The characters in this series are wonderful. Mercy is awesome. </span>
  <span id="freeText15328917638979868715" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a><br /><br />I have so much love for this series! This was my second time reading this book and I can honestly say that I liked it just as much as I did the first and maybe even a bit more. One thing that I enjoy about re-reading books in series that I love is seeing how many things have changed for the characters. I love how some of the groundwork for future events takes root in earlier books.<br /><br />The characters in this series are wonderful. Mercy is awesome. She has a wonderful sense of humor and she is tough. She knows that she is not as physically strong as many of the people she surrounds herself with but she more than makes up for it in mental toughness. She isn't afraid to take risks especially if it is the right thing to do. This book actually has a pretty big cast of characters and I really love them all. Adam and Sam are both great characters. The members of Adam's pack are all so well defined that they really stand out as individuals. I think it takes real skill to bring such a big group of characters to life.<br /><br />The world building in this series is phenomenal. Everything just fits perfectly. It seems like each book adds another layer to the whole picture with complete consistency. I love all of the pack politics and learning about how all of these different groups have learned to live with each other. There were moments in this book that were quite creepy and I loved every moment of it.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Lorelei King's narration. Her voice fits Mercy's character quiet well. It was really easy to follow and I thought she did a great job differentiating between all of the different characters. I also thought that she did a great job in displaying all of the different emotions of the story. I can't wait to continue this series in audio.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this series to others. I think that anyone who enjoys urban fiction or paranormal stories should check out this series. I am a huge Patricia Briggs fan and can't wait to see what she can come up with next. <br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />This was a re-read for me. I love this series and I think that I might have liked this book even more the second time around. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15328917638979868715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
